"Let's think step by step\n1. The cost of each pack of DVDs is 76 dollars.\n2. There is a discount of 25 dollars on each pack.\n3. To find out how much you have to pay after the discount, we subtract the discount from the original cost.\n4. Therefore, the amount you have to pay for each pack after the discount is 76 - 25.\n5. Performing the subtraction, we get 76 - 25 = 51.\nTherefore, you have to pay 51 dollars to buy each pack of DVDs after a discount of 25 dollars."

After some children got off, there were 30 children altogether on the bus.\n4. "Let's think step by step\n1. There are 697 girls in the school.\n2. There are 228 more girls than boys.\n3. Let's assume the number of boys is x.\n4. Therefore, the number of girls is x + 228.\n5. The total number of students in the school is 697 (girls) + x (boys).\n6. According to the information given, the total number of students is also equal to the sum of the number of girls and boys: 697 + x = x + 228.\n7. Solving the equation, we get:\n697 + x = x + 228\n697 - 228 = x - x\n469 = 0\nx = 469\n8. Therefore, there are 469 boys in the school."

"Let's think step by step\n1. Faye is placing her pencils into rows with 22 pencils in each row.\n2. She has 6 packs of pencils, and each pack contains 14 pencils.\n3. To find the total number of pencils, we first calculate the number of pencils in the packs. Since each pack has 14 pencils and she has 6 packs, the total number of pencils in the packs is 14 * 6 = 84 pencils.\n4. Next, we calculate the total number of pencils in the rows. Since each row has 22 pencils and we don't know how many rows there are, we can represent the total number of pencils in the rows as 22x.\n5. The total number of pencils Faye has is the sum of the pencils in the packs and the pencils in the rows, which is 84 + 22x.\n6. We know that the total number of pencils Faye has is the same as the total number of pencils in the rows, which is 22x.\n7. Therefore, we can set up the equation 84 + 22x = 22x.\n8. By solving this equation, we find that x = 84.\n9. Finally, we substitute x back into the equation to find the total number of pencils Faye has: 22 * 84 = 1848 pencils.\nThe answer is 1848."

"Let's think step by step\n1. Rachel had to complete 7 pages of math homework.\n2. She had to complete 4 more pages of math homework than reading homework.\n3. Let's assume the number of pages of reading homework she had to complete is x.\n4. Therefore, the number of pages of math homework she had to complete is x + 4.\n5. The total number of pages she had to complete is 7 (math homework) + x (reading homework).\n6. Since the total number of pages she had to complete is 7, we can write the equation as 7 = x + 4 + x.\n7. Simplifying the equation, we get 7 = 2x + 4.\n8. "Let's think step by step:\n1. Helen baked 19 chocolate chip cookies yesterday.\n2. Helen baked 231 raisin cookies this morning.\n3. Helen baked 237 chocolate chip cookies this morning.\n4. To find out how many more chocolate chip cookies Helen baked than raisin cookies, we need to calculate the total number of each type of cookie.\n5. Helen baked a total of 19 + 237 = 256 chocolate chip cookies.\n6. Helen baked a total of 231 raisin cookies.\n7. To find the difference in the number of chocolate chip and raisin cookies, we subtract the number of raisin cookies from the number of chocolate chip cookies.\n8. Therefore, Helen baked 256 - 231 = 25 more chocolate chip cookies than raisin cookies.\nThe answer is 25."
"Let's think step by step\n1. Tiffany found 4 more bags of cans the next day.\n2. In total, she had 8 bags of cans altogether.\n3. To find out how many bags she had on Monday before finding the additional bags, we need to subtract the number of bags she found the next day from the total number of bags.\n4. Therefore, the number of bags she had on Monday is 8 - 4.\n5. Performing the subtraction, we get 8 - 4 = 4.\nTherefore, Tiffany had 4 bags of cans on Monday before finding 4 more bags the next day."
"Let's think step by step\n1. Danny found 30 bottle caps at the park.\n2. Danny threw away 63 old bottle caps.\n3. Danny now has 42 bottle caps in his collection.\n4. To find out how many more bottle caps Danny threw away than those he found at the park, we need to subtract the number of bottle caps he found from the number he threw away.\n5. Therefore, the number of more bottle caps Danny threw away than those he found at the park is 63 - 30.\n6. Performing the subtraction, we get 63 - 30 = 33.\n7. Therefore, Danny threw away 33 more bottle caps than those he found at the park.\nThe answer is 33"
"Let's think step by step:\n1. The recipe calls for 12 cups of sugar and 14 cups of flour.\n2. Mary already put in 10 cups of sugar.\n3. To find out how many more cups of sugar she needs to add, we subtract the cups of sugar she already put in from the total cups of sugar required.\n4. Therefore, she needs to add 12 - 10 = 2 cups of sugar.\n5. To find out how many more cups of flour she needs to add, we subtract the cups of flour required from the cups of flour she already put in.\n6. Therefore, she needs to add 14 - 10 = 4 cups of flour.\n7. The question asks for the difference between the cups of flour and sugar she needs to add now, which is 4 - 2 = 2 cups.\nThe answer is 2 cups."

Therefore, the number of tomatoes he has left after picking is 171 - 134 - 30.\n6. To find out how many more orchids than roses are there now, we need to subtract the initial number of roses and orchids from the current number.\n4. Therefore, the number of more orchids than roses now is (20 - 12) - (11 - 7).\n5. Performing the subtraction, we get (20 - 12) - (11 - 7) = 8 - 4 = 4.\n6. Therefore, there are 4 more orchids than roses in the vase now.\nThe answer is 4."

Therefore, the number of more bottles of regular soda than diet soda is 83 - 54.\n4. Performing the subtraction, we get 83 - 54 = 29.\nTherefore, the grocery store had 29 more bottles of regular soda than diet soda."
"Let's think step by step:\n1. 269 students suggested adding bacon.\n2. 330 students suggested adding mashed potatoes.\n3. To find out how many more students suggested adding mashed potatoes than those that suggested adding bacon, we subtract the number of students who suggested bacon from the number of students who suggested mashed potatoes.\n4. Therefore, the number of more students who suggested adding mashed potatoes than those who suggested adding bacon is 330 - 269.\n5. Performing the subtraction, we get 330 - 269 = 61.\nTherefore, 61 more students suggested adding mashed potatoes than those that suggested adding bacon."
"Let's think step by step\n1. Brenda's mother made cookies for 14 people.\n2. Each person received 30 cookies.\n3. To find out how many cookies Brenda's mother prepared in total, we need to multiply the number of people by the number of cookies each person received.\n4. Therefore, the total number of cookies prepared is 14 * 30.\n5. Performing the multiplication, we get 14 * 30 = 420.\nTherefore, Brenda's mother prepared 420 cookies in total."
"Let's think step by step:\n1. Dave had 15 apps on his phone.\n2. He added 71 new apps.\n3. After deleting some, he had 14 apps left.\n4. To find out how many more apps he deleted than he added, we need to calculate the total number of apps he had after adding and then subtract the number of apps he had left.\n5. The total number of apps after adding is 15 + 71 = 86.\n6. Dave deleted 86 - 14 = 72 apps.\n7. Therefore, Dave deleted 72 - 71 = 1 more app than he added.\nThe answer is 1."

To find out how many crackers each friend ate, we need to subtract the crackers Matthew had left from the total number of crackers he started with.\n5. Therefore, the total number of sacks of oranges left after 51 days of harvest is 3 * 51 = 153.\nThe answer is 153."

"Let's think step by step:\n1. The grasshopper jumped 19 inches.\n2. The grasshopper jumped 4 inches farther than the frog.\n3. Let's assume the distance the frog jumped is x inches.\n4. Therefore, the grasshopper jumped x + 4 inches.\n5. The mouse jumped 44 inches lesser than the frog, which means the mouse jumped x - 44 inches.\n6. Given that the total distance jumped by all three is the sum of their individual jumps, we have: 19 (grasshopper) + x (frog) + x + 4 (frog) + x - 44 (mouse) = total distance.\n7. Simplifying the equation, we get: 19 + 2x - 40 = total distance.\n8. Combining like terms, we get: 2x - 21 = total distance.\n9. Since the total distance is the sum of all three jumps, we can substitute the total distance with 19 + x + x + 4 + x - 44.\n10. Solving the equation, we get: 2x - 21 = 19 + 3x - 40.\n11. Simplifying further, we get: 2x - 21 = 3x - 21.\n12. Rearranging the equation, we get: x = 21.\nTherefore, the frog jumped 21 inches in the jumping contest."

Therefore, the number of more bird families that flew to Africa than those that flew to Asia is 62 - 35.\n6. Performing the subtraction, we get 62 - 35 = 27.\nTherefore, 27 more bird families flew away to Africa than those that flew to Asia."
"Let's think step by step\n1. Paul got a box of 65 crayons for his birthday.\n2. He gave 213 crayons to his friends during the school year.\n3. He lost 16 crayons.\n4. To find out how many crayons Paul lost or gave away, we add the number of crayons he gave away to his friends and the number of crayons he lost.\n5. Therefore, the total number of crayons lost or given away is 213 + 16.\n6. Performing the addition, we get 213 + 16 = 229.\n7. Therefore, Paul lost or gave away a total of 229 crayons during the school year.\nThe answer is 229"

Since each of them had the same number of cookies, we need to divide the total number of cookies they had by the number of people.\n5. "Let's think step by step\n1. Ryan spends 6 hours learning English every day.\n2. Ryan spends 7 hours learning Chinese every day.\n3. To find out how many hours he spends on learning English and Chinese in total over 5 days, we need to calculate the total hours for each language and then add them together.\n4. For learning English, he spends 6 hours per day for 5 days, so the total hours spent on learning English is 6 * 5 = 30 hours.\n5. For learning Chinese, he spends 7 hours per day for 5 days, so the total hours spent on learning Chinese is 7 * 5 = 35 hours.\n6. Adding the total hours for learning English and Chinese, we get 30 + 35 = 65 hours.\nTherefore, Ryan spends a total of 65 hours on learning English and Chinese over 5 days."

"Let's think step by step\n1. Adam and Jackie have 12 apples together.\n2. He has 9 apples more than Adam and Jackie together do.\n3. Adam has 8 more apples than Jackie.\n4. Let's denote the number of apples Adam has as A, Jackie has as J, and He has as H.\n5. From the information given, we can form the following equations:\n   A + J = 12 (Adam and Jackie have 12 apples together)\n   H = A + J + 9 (He has 9 apples more than Adam and Jackie together)\n   A = J + 8 (Adam has 8 more apples than Jackie)\n6. Substituting the third equation into the first equation, we get:\n   J + 8 + J = 12\n   2J + 8 = 12\n   2J = 4\n   J = 2\n7. Substituting J = 2 into A = J + 8, we get:\n   A = 2 + 8\n   A = 10\n8. Substituting J = 2 and A = 10 into H = A + J + 9, we get:\n   H = 10 + 2 + 9\n   H = 21\nTherefore, He has 21 apples."

"Let's think step by step:\n1. The grasshopper jumped 21 inches.\n2. The grasshopper jumped 25 inches farther than the frog.\n3. The mouse jumped 16 inches lesser than the frog.\n4. To find out how far the frog jumped, we need to subtract the additional distance the grasshopper jumped from the total distance the grasshopper jumped.\n5. Therefore, the frog jumped 21 - 25 = -4 inches. (Negative value indicates the frog jumped 4 inches less than the grasshopper)\n6. To find out how far the mouse jumped, we need to subtract the distance the mouse jumped from the distance the frog jumped.\n7. Therefore, the mouse jumped -4 - 16 = -20 inches. (Negative value indicates the mouse jumped 20 inches less than the frog)\n8. To find out how much farther the grasshopper jumped than the mouse, we need to subtract the distance the mouse jumped from the distance the grasshopper jumped.\n9. Therefore, the grasshopper jumped 21 - (-20) = 21 + 20 = 41 inches farther than the mouse.\nThe answer is 41 inches."

"Let's think step by step\n1. 62 campers went rowing in the morning.\n2. 39 campers went rowing in the afternoon.\n3. To find out how many more campers went rowing in the morning than in the afternoon, we subtract the number of campers in the afternoon from the number in the morning.\n4. Therefore, the number of more campers in the morning than in the afternoon is 62 - 39.\n5. Performing the subtraction, we get 62 - 39 = 23.\nTherefore, 23 more campers went rowing in the morning than in the afternoon."
"Let's think step by step\n1. There are 315 girls in the school.\n2. There are 309 boys in the school.\n3. There are 772 teachers in the school.\n4. To find the total number of people in the school, we need to add the number of girls, boys, and teachers together.\n5. Therefore, the total number of people in the school is 315 (girls) + 309 (boys) + 772 (teachers).\n6. Adding these numbers together, we get 315 + 309 + 772 = 1396.\nTherefore, there are 1396 people in the school, including students and teachers."

To find out how many boys she gave marbles to, we need to divide the total number of marbles by the number of marbles given to each boy.\n4. Therefore, the number of boys she gave marbles to is 10 / 5.\n5. Performing the division, we get 10 / 5 = 2.\n6. Therefore, Haley gave the marbles to 2 boys.\nThe answer is 2"

To find out how much money he earns during the harvest season, we need to calculate the total earnings from regular work and overtime work.\n4. Total earnings from regular work = $28/week * 1091 weeks = $30588\n5. Total earnings from overtime work = $939/week * 1091 weeks = $1024749\n6. Therefore, the total amount of money Lewis earns during the harvest season is $30588 + $1024749 = $1055337\nThe answer is $1055337"

"Let's think step by step\n1. Paige and her mom planted 36 seeds in total.\n2. They put 12 seeds in each flower bed.\n3. Only 58 seeds grew into flowers in each flower bed.\n4. To find out how many flower beds they had, we need to divide the total number of seeds by the number of seeds in each flower bed that grew into flowers.\n5. Therefore, the number of flower beds they had is 36 / 58.\n6. Performing the division, we get 36 / 58 = 0.62 (rounded to two decimal places).\n7. Since we can't have a fraction of a flower bed, we need to round up to the nearest whole number.\n8. Therefore, Paige and her mom had 1 flower bed.\nThe answer is 1."
